Defining Haqiqah and Majaz: Literal and Metaphorical Usage in Hanafi Usul
Defines haqiqah and majaz with conditions and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise definitions of haqiqah and majaz, identify the condition of suitability (munasaba), and apply the aspect qualification (haythiyya) to distinguish between literal and metaphorical usage.

Core Idea
Haqiqah uses a word for its original assignment; majaz uses it for another due to suitability, both defined by the aspect of usage.

Understanding haqiqah (literal) and majaz (metaphorical) is foundational to Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The correct interpretation of Qur'anic and Hadith texts depends on recognizing when a word is used literally or figuratively. This lesson unpacks the precise definitions from a classical Hanafi text, clarifying the conditions and the role of speaker intent versus listener comprehension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary terms
Recognize that haqiqah and majaz are attributes of usage (isti'mal), not intrinsic properties of words. They are defined relative to the word's original assignment (wad').
Both are 'accidents of words' (ʿawāriḍ al-alfāẓ).
2
Understand the role of wad' (assignment)
Haqiqah relies on linguistic, shar'i, or customary assignment. Majaz lacks that assignment in the intended meaning.
Hanafi usul recognizes three types of wad'.
3
Grasp the condition of suitability (munasaba)
For majaz, a relationship must exist between the original and intended meanings. This excludes arbitrary misuse or jest.
Example: using 'earth' for 'sky' has no suitability.
4
Apply the aspect qualification (haythiyya)
The definitions must include 'from the aspect that it is its assignment' (for haqiqah) or 'from the aspect that it is not its assignment' (for majaz) to avoid circularity.
This precision distinguishes the two concepts.
5
Recognize the exclusion of qarinah from the core definition
The contextual indicator (qarinah) is for listener understanding, not part of the essential definition of majaz. It will be discussed later in the text.
Speaker's intent suffices for the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان المتقابلات للأقسام الأربعة السابقة
تعريف المجاز وحكمه
وإلا فوضع عرفي عام والمعتبر في الحقيقة هو الوضع بشيء من الأوضاع المذكورة، وفي المجاز عدمه، فهما في الحقيقة من عوارض الألفاظ، وقد يوصف بهما المعاني، والاستعمال إما مجازا أو على أنه من خطأ العوام. وحكمها وجود ما وضع له خاصا كان أو عاما، فإن الحقيقة تجتمع مع الخاص والعام جميعًا، فإن قوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ارْكَعُوا﴾ (الحج : ۷۷) وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَقْرَبُوا الزِّني﴾ (الإسراء: ۳۲) خاص باعتبار الفعل وهو الركوع والزنا، وعام باعتبار الفاعل وهم المكلفون.
وأما المجاز فاسم لما أريد به غير ما وضع له لمناسبة بينهما أي اسم لكل لفظ أريد به أي بقيد المناسبة غير ما وضع له لأجل مناسبة بين المعنى الموضوع له وغير الموضوع له، واحترز به عن مثل استعمال لفظ الأرض في السماء مما لا مناسبة بينهما، وعن الهزل، فإنه وإن أريد غير ما وضع له لكن لا مناسبة بينهما، ولم يذكر قيد كونه عند قيام قرينة؛ لأن الغرض ههنا بيان المجاز بحسب إرادة المتكلم وقد تم به، والقرينة إنما يحتاج إليها لأجل فهم السامع وهو أمر زائد على أنه سيأتي ذكرها في آخر بحث المجاز، وأما المجاز بالزيادة مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ﴾ (الشورى: ۱۱) فيصدق عليه أيضا أنه أريد به غير ما وضع له؛ لأن ما وضع له الكاف هو التشبيه لا التأكيد أو الزيادة فيدخل في التعريف، ولكن لابد في تعريف الحقيقة والمجاز كليهما من قيد الحيثية أي من حيث أنه ما وضع له أو غير ما وضع له؛ فالحقيقة لفظ مستعمل فيما وضع له من حيث أنه ما وضع له، والمجاز لفظ مستعمل في غير ما وضع له من حيث أنه غير ما وضع له. (القمر)
Statement of opposites for the previous four divisions. Definition of Majaz and its ruling: Otherwise, it is a general customary assignment, and what is considered in haqiqah (literal usage) is assignment by some of the mentioned assignments, and in majaz (metaphorical usage) its absence. So they are both essentially accidents of words, and they may be attributed to meanings. Usage is either metaphorical or such that it is from the error of the common people. Their ruling is the existence of what it was assigned for, whether specific or general. Verily, haqiqah combines with both specific and general. For His statement, 'O you who have believed, bow' (Quran 22:77) and His statement, 'And do not approach zina (adultery)' (Quran 17:32) are specific with respect to the action, which is bowing and zina, and general with respect to the agent, who are the legally responsible. As for majaz, it is a name for what is intended by other than what it was assigned for, due to a suitability between them. That is, it is a name for every word intended, with the condition of suitability, for other than what it was assigned for, due to a suitability between the meaning assigned for and the meaning not assigned for. By this, it avoids the likes of using the word 'earth' to mean 'sky' where there is no suitability between them, and also avoids jest, for even if it intends other than what it was assigned for, there is no suitability. The condition of the existence of a contextual indicator is not mentioned because the purpose here is to explain majaz in terms of the speaker's intent, and that completes it. The contextual indicator is only needed for the listener's understanding, which is an additional matter; moreover, it will be mentioned later at the end of the discussion of majaz. As for majaz by addition, like His statement, 'There is nothing like Him' (Quran 42:11), it also applies to it that it intends other than what it was assigned for, because what the letter 'kaf' was assigned for is comparison, not emphasis or addition, so it enters the definition. But it is necessary in the definition of both haqiqah and majaz to include the qualification of aspect, i.e., from the aspect that it is what it was assigned for or not what it was assigned for. Thus haqiqah is a word used for what it was assigned for from the aspect that it is what it was assigned for, and majaz is a word used for other than what it was assigned for from the aspect that it is other than what it was assigned for. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the definitions of haqiqah and majaz from a Hanafi usul text. The commentator begins by clarifying that haqiqah is based on linguistic, shar'i, or customary assignment (wad'), while majaz lacks this assignment in the intended meaning. Both are attributes of words, not meanings, though they can describe meanings. The ruling of haqiqah is that the meaning assigned is affirmed; it combines with both specific and general usages, as shown in Quranic examples where the verb 'bow' and 'do not approach' are specific in action but general in audience. The definition of majaz requires a word used for other than its original meaning due to a clear suitability (munasaba) between the original and intended meanings. This excludes arbitrary misuses like calling earth 'sky' or jest, where no suitability exists. The contextual indicator (qarinah) is not part of the core definition because it pertains to the listener's understanding, but it will be discussed later. The commentator also addresses majaz by addition (e.g., the extra 'kaf' in 'laysa kamithlihi shay') which fits the definition as the added element is not used for its original comparative sense. Finally, to avoid circularity, the definitions must include a qualification of aspect (haythiyya): haqiqah uses a word for its original meaning precisely because it is that meaning, and majaz uses it for another meaning precisely because it is not the original. This precision distinguishes the two concepts clearly.

Key Terms
الحقيقة (al-ḥaqīqah): لفظ مستعمل فيما وضع له من حيث أنه ما وضع له (a word used for what it was assigned for, from the aspect that it is its assignment)
المجاز (al-majāz): لفظ مستعمل في غير ما وضع له لمناسبة بينهما من حيث أنه غير ما وضع له (a word used for other than its original assignment due to a suitability between them, from the aspect that it is not its assignment)
الوضع (al-waḍ'): تخصيص اللفظ بالمعنى (assigning a word to a meaning) by linguistic, shar'i, or customary convention
الاستعمال (al-isti'māl): استخدام اللفظ في المعنى (using a word for a meaning)
القرينة (al-qarīnah): دليل سياقي يفهم منه إرادة المعنى المجازي (contextual indicator from which the intended metaphorical meaning is understood) - mentioned as to be discussed later

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling (hukm) of haqiqah (literal usage)?
A) It is invalid and must be avoided.
B) It is permissible but not necessary.
C) It affirms the existence of the assigned meaning.
D) It requires a contextual indicator (qarinah) to be understood.

Key Takeaway
The precise definitions of haqiqah and majaz depend on the aspect of usage (haythiyya) and the presence of suitability, not on contextual indicators.

Definition of Majaz and the Necessity of Haythiyya
Defines majaz and argues for the haythiyya qualification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the essential components of the Hanafi definition of majaz and explain why the haythiyya qualification is required to prevent logical contradiction in definitions.

Core Idea
Majaz requires a relationship between meanings; the haythiyya is essential to keep haqiqa and majaz definitions exclusive.

In Hanafi usul, the definition of majaz is not just 'used for other than its original meaning'—it requires a genuine relationship between the meanings. Furthermore, to avoid a logical flaw where the same word could be both haqiqa and majaz simultaneously, the scholars introduced the subtle but crucial qualification of 'haythiyya' (aspectuality). This lesson unpacks both elements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definition
The text defines majaz as 'usage other than what it is placed for, due to a relationship between the original meaning and the non-original meaning.' Isolate the three components: non-original usage, relationship, and exclusion of cases without relationship.
The definition is from the speaker's intention; qarina (contextual clue) is not part because it is for the listener.
2
Understand what is excluded
The definition explicitly excludes using 'earth' for 'sky' (no relationship) and jest (hazl) even if it intends another meaning, because there is no genuine relationship. Note that hazl is excluded despite intent.
Jest lacks the relationship (munasaba) required for valid majaz.
3
Recognize the definitional problem
Without the haythiyya qualification, a word like 'salat' could be both haqiqa (linguistic meaning 'supplication') and majaz (legal meaning 'pillars') from different perspectives, causing definitions to lose exclusivity (tard wa 'aks).
The text uses the example of 'salat' to illustrate the overlap.
4
Apply the haythiyya solution
The haythiyya adds 'from the aspect that it is what it is placed for' or 'from the aspect that it is not placed for'. This makes each definition true only under its specific aspect, resolving contradiction.
E.g., linguistically 'salat' is haqiqa in supplication and majaz in pillars; legally the reverse.
5
Generalise the ruling
The text states that majaz has the same legal capacity as haqiqa: it can be specific or general. But 'general' here means encompassing individuals within one type, not all relationships simultaneously.
Example: using 'sa'a' (a measure) to refer to all that is measured in it is permissible.

Source Text

تعريف المجاز وحكمه
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث غير ما وضع له لأجل مناسبة بين المعنى الموضوع له وغير الموضوع له، واحترز به عن مثل استعمال لفظ الأرض في السماء مما لا مناسبة بينهما، وعن الهزل، فإنه وإن أريد غير ما وضع له لكن لا مناسبة بينهما، ولم يذكر قيد كونه عند قيام قرينة؛ لأن الغرض ههنا بيان المجاز بحسب إرادة المتكلم وقد تم به، والقرينة إنما يحتاج إليها لأجل فهم السامع وهو أمر زائد على أنه سيأتي ذكرها في آخر بحث المجاز ، وأما المجاز بالزيادة مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَيْسَ كَمِثْلِهِ شَيْءٌ﴾ فيصدق عليه أيضا أنه أريد به غير ما وضع له؛ لأن ما وضع له هو التشبيه لا التأكيد أو الزيادة فيدخل في التعريف، ولكن لابد في تعريف الحقيقة والمجاز كليهما من قيد الحيثية أي من حيث أنه ما وضع له أو غير ما وضع له؛ لئلا ينتقض التعريفان طردًا وعكسا ، فإن لفظ الصلاة في اللغة: للدعاء، وفي الشرع: للأركان المعلومة، فهي من حيث اللغة حقيقة في الدعاء؛ لأنه يصدق عليه أنه ما وضع له من حيث أنه ما وضع له، ومجاز في الأركان؛ لأنه غير ما وضع له من حيث أنه غير ما وضع له في الجملة، ومن حيث الشرع حقيقة في الأركان؛ لأنها ما وضع له من حيث أنها ما وضع له ومجاز في الدعاء؛ لأنه غير ما وضع له من حيث أنه غير ما وضع له في الجملة. وحكمه وجود ما استعير له خاصا كان أو عاما أن المجاز كالحقيقة في كونه خاصا أو عاما، وليس المراد بكون المجاز عاما أن يعم جميع أنواع علاقاته جملة في لفظ بأن يذكر اللفظ ویراد به حاله ومحله وما كان عليه وما يؤل إليه ولازمه وعلته ومعلوله ونحو ذلك، بل أن يعم جميع أفراد نوع واحد كما يراد بالصاع جميع ما يحلّ فيه، فيجوز ذلك عندنا.

(القمر) فيدخل إلخ : أي المجاز بالزيادة في تعريف المجاز لكنه يخدشه أن الاتصال شرط للمجاز على ما سيجيء، ولا اتصال بين التشبيه والتأكيد كذا قيل فتأمل. (القمر)
من قيد إلخ إلا أنه كثيرًا ما يحذف من اللفظ بوضوحه خصوصا عند تعلق الحكم بالوصف المشعر بالعلية كذا في "التلويح" . (القمر) من قيد الحيثية : وإنما تركه المصنف للشهرة والظهور (القمر) .

لئلا ينتقض التعريفان طردًا وعكسا ، فإن لفظ الصلاة في اللغة: للدعاء، وفي الشرع: للأركان المعلومة، فهي من حيث اللغة حقيقة في الدعاء؛ لأنه يصدق عليه أنه ما وضع له من حيث أنه ما وضع له، ومجاز في الأركان؛ لأنه غير ما وضع له من حيث أنه غير ما وضع له في الجملة، ومن حيث الشرع حقيقة في الأركان؛ لأنها ما وضع له من حيث أنها ما وضع له ومجاز في الدعاء؛ لأنه غير ما وضع له من حيث أنه غير ما وضع له في الجملة. وحكمه وجود ما استعير له خاصا كان أو عاما أن المجاز كالحقيقة في كونه خاصا أو عاما. وليس المراد بكون المجاز عاما أن يعم جميع أنواع علاقاته جملة في لفظ بأن يذكر اللفظ ویراد به حاله ومحله وما كان عليه وما يؤل إليه ولازمه وعلته ومعلوله ونحو ذلك، بل أن يعم جميع أفراد نوع واحد كما يراد بالصاع جميع ما يحلّ فيه، فيجوز ذلك عندنا.

(القمر) خاصا كان إلخ: قد سبق في حد الخاص أن المراد بالوضع أعم من الشخصي والنوعي والمجاز موضوع بالوضع فلا ينافي كونه خاصا أو عاما. (السنبلي) خاصا وعامًا إلخ: يعني أن المستعار له إذا كان عاما يثبت العموم فيه، وإن كان اللفظ خاصا لا يقال: كيف يثبت العموم بلفظ خاص؛ لأنه يمكن ذلك كما في لفظ القوم والرهط (السنبلي) أنواع علاقاته إلخ : سيجيء منا ذكر أنواع العلاقات، فانتظره. (القمر)
Definition of majaz and its ruling. Explanation of the sections of the third division: [usage] other than what it is placed for, due to a relationship between the original meaning and the non-original meaning. By this, he excludes expressions like using the word 'earth' for 'sky' where there is no relationship between them, and also excludes jest (hazl), because even though it intends other than what it is placed for, there is no relationship. He did not mention the condition of being with a contextual clue (qarina) because the purpose here is to explain majaz according to the speaker's intention, and that is complete with this; the qarina is needed only for the listener's understanding, which is additional, and it will be mentioned later. As for majaz by addition (majaz bi al-ziyada), like His saying: {There is nothing like Him} (Shura 11), it is also true that the intended meaning is other than what the word is placed for; because what it is placed for is comparison (tashbih), not affirmation or addition, so it enters the definition. However, in defining both haqiqa and majaz, the qualification of 'aspectuality' (haythiyya) is necessary, i.e., from the aspect that it is what it is placed for or other than what it is placed for, so that the two definitions do not invalidate each other in terms of comprehensiveness and exclusivity. For example, the word 'salat' in language means 'supplication' and in law means 'the known pillars'; from the language perspective it is haqiqa in supplication because it applies to it as what it is placed for from that aspect, and majaz in the pillars because it is other than what it is placed for from that aspect. Similarly, from the legal perspective it is haqiqa in the pillars and majaz in supplication. Its ruling is that the existence of what is borrowed (musta'ar lahu), whether specific or general, is that majaz is like haqiqa in being specific or general. It is not meant by 'majaz being general' that it encompasses all types of relationships comprehensively in one word such that the word is mentioned and intended to refer to its state, its locus, what it was upon, what it leads to, its necessary concomitant, its cause, its effect, etc. Rather, it means encompassing all individuals of one type, like intending by 'sa'a' all that is measured in it; this is permissible according to us. [Marginal glosses follow.]
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a definition of majaz (metaphorical usage) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by clarifying that majaz is using a word for something other than its original meaning, but only if there is a relationship (munasaba) between the original and the new meaning. This excludes cases like using 'earth' for 'sky' (no relationship) and jest (hazl) where the speaker does not mean what the word signifies but no relationship exists. He then notes that he did not include the condition of a contextual clue (qarina) because at this point he is defining majaz from the speaker's intention; the qarina is necessary for the listener's understanding and will be discussed later. He also addresses 'majaz bi al-ziyada' (metaphor by addition) like the extra 'kaaf' in 'laysa kamithlihi shay' which indicates affirmation, not comparison—such usage is also metaphorical because the word is used for something other than its original placement. A critical point follows: to properly define both haqiqa and majaz without contradictions, we must add the qualification 'min haythu annahu' (from the aspect that it is). Without this, definitions could overlap; for example, the word 'salat' is haqiqa in its linguistic meaning (supplication) and majaz in its legal meaning, but from the legal perspective it is the opposite. By adding 'from the aspect that it is placed for it' or 'from the aspect that it is not placed for it', we ensure that each definition is clearly distinguished. The passage then discusses the ruling of majaz: that it can be specific or general like haqiqa, but 'general' here does not mean using one word to indicate all possible relationships simultaneously; rather, it means the borrowed meaning can be general in its individuals, like using 'sa'a' (a specific measure) to refer to all that is measured in it, which is permissible in the Hanafi school. The marginal glosses (from al-Qamar and al-Sunbuli) provide further explanation: they clarify why the qualification is needed, how to apply it to the example of 'salat', and discuss the concept of 'tard' and 'aks' (comprehensiveness and exclusivity) in definitions.

Key Terms
المجاز (al-majāz): A word used for other than its original meaning due to a relationship, with the aspect of being other than its original meaning.
الحيثية (al-ḥaythiyya): Aspectuality; the qualification 'from the aspect that it is' added to definitions to ensure they are mutually exclusive.
المناسبة (al-munāsaba): A relationship between the original and metaphorical meaning that justifies the figurative usage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the qualification 'min haythu annahu' (from the aspect that it is) necessary in the definitions of haqiqa and majaz?
A) To exclude metaphorical usage by addition.
B) To prevent the definitions from contradicting each other in comprehensiveness and exclusivity, as seen in the example of 'salat'.
C) To ensure that the contextual clue (qarina) is always present.
D) To allow haqiqa and majaz to be used interchangeably.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of majaz requires a relationship between meanings, and the haythiyya qualification is essential to prevent definitional overlap between haqiqa and majaz.

Impossibility of Combining Haqiqah and Majaz in One Word
Stating the usul rule with dispute and example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on combining haqiqah and majaz in one word, explain the reasoning behind it, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
One word cannot simultaneously carry literal and metaphorical intended meanings in Hanafi usul.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Anwar states a fundamental usul rule: it is impossible for a single word to intend both its literal and metaphorical meanings at the same time. This rule has practical implications for interpreting texts and resolving apparent conflicts. We will unpack the rule, examine the example of the word 'lion,' and see how the Shafi'i school disagrees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'It is impossible for both meanings to be intended by a single word.' Note that this applies when the speaker intends both meanings simultaneously as objects of the ruling.
The rule does not apply when two separate words are used, or when one meaning is primary and the other is secondary via kinayah.
2
Analyze the example: 'Do not kill the lion'
Consider the word 'asd' (lion). If one says 'Do not kill the lion' meaning both the predatory animal and a brave man, this would be combining haqiqah and majaz. The Hanafi school says this is impossible.
The Shafi'i school allows it if the two meanings can coexist, as in this example.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The rule stems from the fact that a word cannot be both literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) at the same time. The metaphorical usage requires a qarina (contextual clue) that shifts from the literal meaning, making simultaneous intention contradictory.
This is linked to the broader issue of using a word with multiple meanings (ishtirak) in a single context.
4
Distinguish from the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i held that if the two meanings can be combined without contradiction, it is permissible. The Hanafis reject this because the word's relationship to the literal meaning changes when used metaphorically.
The dispute traces back to whether a word used metaphorically can still carry its literal sense simultaneously.
5
Apply the rule to other examples
Consider the command 'Do X.' Can it mean both obligation and permission? The Hanafis say no, because these are contradictory. The Shafi'is allow it only if the meanings are compatible.
Think of cases where a single word has multiple plausible interpretations; the rule guides which interpretations are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث ٢٧٥ بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز] ويستحيل اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظ واحد من تتمة السابق أي يستحيل اجتماع المعنى الحقيقي والمعنى المجازي حال كونهما مرادين بلفظ واحد بأن يكون كل منهما متعلق الحكم كأن تقول: "لا تقتل "الأسد" وتريد السبع والرجل الشجاع معا، وإن كان اللفظ بالنظر إلى هذا الاستعمال مجازا، وقد صححه الشافعي مطالبه حيث يمكن الجمع بينهما كما في هذا المثال، بخلاف ما إذا لم يمكن كالوجوب والإباحة في الأمر، . من اجتماعها الضمير راجع إلى الحقيقة والمجاز بإرادة المعنى الحقيقي والمجازي على طور صنعة الاستخدام، فإن الحقيقة والمجاز يطلقان على المعاني أيضًا. (القمر) مرادين: أي مقصودين بالحكم. [إفاضة الأنوار: ١٠١] تتمة السابق فإنه من أحكام الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) من تتمة السابق إلخ جواب سؤال يرد على المصنف بأنه بصد ورد الخصم، وهو لا يحصل؛ لأن الحقيقة والمجاز من صفات الألفاظ، ولا يجوز كون اللفظ الواحد حقيقة ومجازا معًا بالاتفاق وتقرير :الجواب: أن هذا الكلام ليس ردًا للخصم، بل هو حكم آخر للحقيقة والمجاز، والضمير في اجتماعهما ليس راجعا إلى نفس الحقيقة والمجاز، بل إليهما مع حذف المضاف أي معنى الحقيقة ومعنى المجاز ويحصل في ضمنه ترديد الخصم أيضًا؛ لأن الشافعي الله يجوز اجتماع معناهما مرادين بلفظ واحد وإن لم يجز كون اللفظ الواحد حقيقة ومجازا معًا فتدبر (السنبلي حال كونهما إلخ إيماء إلى أن قول المصنف مرادين حال.(القمر) حال كونهما مرادين إلخ فيه احتراز عن اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظين، وما ذكر في "الذخيرة" يدل عليه وهو: أن الرجل إذا قال: إن دخلت دار زيد فامرأتي طالق، وإن دخلت دار عمرو فعبدي ،حر، فدخل دارًا مملوكة لزيد قد سكنها عمرو بإجارة أو إعارة يحنث في اليمين وفيه جمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز في لفظين. (السنبلي) بأن يكون كل منهما إلخ أي لا المجموع من حيث المجموع، ولا واحد منهما، واحترز به عن الكناية؛ فإن مناط الحكم في الكناية إنما هو المعنى الثاني كذا في "التلويح". (القمر) وتريد السبع والرجل إلخ : أحدهما بسبب أنه موضوع له، وثانيهما بسبب أنه مناسب للموضوع له. (القمر) وقد صححه الشافعي له إلخ وهذا الاختلاف فرع الاختلاف في استعمال المشترك في تعيينه، فإن اللفظ موضوع للمعنى المجازي بالوضع النوعي، فهو بالنظر إلى الوضعين بمنزلة المشترك، فمن جوز ذلك جوز هذا، ومن لا فلا كذا في "التلويح". (السنبلي)
Statement on the impossibility of combining the literal and metaphorical meanings: It is impossible for both meanings to be intended by a single word, meaning it is impossible for the literal meaning and the metaphorical meaning together to be intended by a single word, each being the object of the ruling, such as when you say: 'Do not kill the lion' intending both the beast and the brave man together, even though the word in this usage is metaphorical. Al-Shafi'i has validated this where combining them is possible as in this example, unlike where it is impossible as obligation and permissibility in the command.
Source pages p. 276

Commentary
This passage states a usul rule: it is impossible to intend both the literal and metaphorical meanings of a word in a single utterance. The author explains that 'haqiqah' and 'majaz' here refer to the meanings themselves, not the linguistic categories. The example given is the word 'asd' (lion): if one says 'do not kill the lion' intending both the predatory animal and a brave man, that is combining two meanings. The Shafi'i school allows this when such combination is possible, but the Hanafis reject it. The commentary clarifies that this impossibility concerns a single word being used to convey both meanings simultaneously; however, combining them in different words is allowed, as shown by an example from al-Dhakhirah involving conditional oaths. It also distinguishes from kinayah (allusion) where the ruling is based on the second meaning only. The dispute is linked to the broader issue of using a word with multiple meanings (ishtirak) in a single context.

Key Terms
حَقِيقَة (ḥaqīqah): Literal meaning; the original meaning for which the word was coined.
مَجَاز (majāz): Metaphorical meaning; usage of a word for a meaning other than its original with a qarina.
اسْتِحَالَة (istiḥālah): Impossibility; the rule that combining the literal and metaphorical meanings in one word is impossible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on using a single word to mean both its literal and metaphorical meanings simultaneously?
A) It is allowed if there is no contradiction
B) It is impossible
C) It is allowed only in oaths
D) It is recommended

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a single word cannot simultaneously convey both its literal and metaphorical intended meanings; only one can be meant per utterance.

Combining Haqiqah and Majaz: The Garment Analogy and Application to Bequests
Explains the principle that haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined, with a branch example on wills.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined, and derive the fiqh ruling for a bequest using the word 'mawali'.

Core Idea
A word cannot be literal and figurative at once — just as one garment cannot be owned and borrowed simultaneously.

This lesson explains a key Hanafi usul principle using a vivid garment analogy and applies it to a real fiqh issue: wills involving the term 'mawali'. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly interpreting legal texts and resolving apparent conflicts between literal and figurative meanings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source text and operative term
Focus on the phrase 'al-wasiyyatu lil-mawali' from the passage, where 'mawali' is the key term. It is homonymous, meaning both 'liberator' (mu'tiq) and 'freed slave' (mu'taq) literally, and figuratively for the liberator's liberator.
2
Classify the word's usage
Determine that for 'mu'tiq', the word is haqiqah (literal), and for 'mu'tiq's mu'tiq', it is majaz (figurative). This classification is based on the degree of directness in the relationship.
The Hanafi view holds that the literal meaning is primary and the figurative is secondary.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul rule
Recall the principle: haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined in a single utterance. This is proven by analogy: a garment cannot be owned and borrowed by two persons at the same time. Therefore, in a bequest, only one of the two meanings can be intended.
The Shafi'i objection (that the word is merely majaz when both are intended) is addressed by showing that even then, the usage in each sense would have to be both, which is impossible.
4
Derive the fiqh ruling
When a testator bequests to 'mawali' and has one mu'tiq (liberator) and one mu'tiq's mu'tiq, only the literal meaning (mu'tiq) is given effect. The mu'tiq gets half of the bequest (since the minimum of mawali is two), and the mu'tiq's mu'tiq receives nothing.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) include the mu'tiq's mu'tiq due to the generality of majaz.
5
Note cross-madhhab and intra-madhhab differences
The Shafi'i school would consider the word majaz in both senses, potentially including both parties. The intra-Hanafi difference with the Sahibayn shows that even within the school, the application of this principle can vary.
The mufta bihi position adopted in this text is Abu Hanifa's, as stated in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز يعني أن اللفظ للمعنى بمنزلة اللباس للشخص، والمجاز كالثوب المستعار، والحقيقة كالثوب المملوك، فكما أن استعمال الثوب الواحد في حالة واحدة بطريق الملك والعارية جميعا محال كذلك استعمال اللفظ الواحد بطريق الحقيقة والمجاز محال، والأوضح في المثال أن يقول: كما استحال أن يلبس الثوب الواحد اللابسان أحدهما بطريق الملك والآخر بطريق العارية في زمان واحد ليكون اللفظ بمنزلة اللباس والمعنيان بمنزلة اللابسين، والحقيقة والمجاز بمنزلة الملك والعارية، ولا يقال : إن الراهن إذا استعار الثوب المرهون من المرتهن ولبسه يصدق عليه أنه البسه بطريق الملك والعارية جميعًا؛ لأنا نقول: إن لبسه هذا ليس بطريق العارية؛ لأن المرتمن لم يتملك الثوب حتى يعيره الراهن، ولكنه بطريق الملك؛ لأن حق المرتمن كان مانعا، فلا كذلك استعمال إلخ: اعترض عليه من جانب الشافعي له بأنا لا نجعل اللفظ عند إرادة المعنى الحقيقي والمجازي حقيقة ومجازا ليكون استعماله فيهما بمنزلة استعمال الثوب بطريق الملك والعارية، بل نجعله مجازا فقط، فإنه مستعمل في كل واحد، وهو غير الموضوع له فتأمل (القمر) والأوضح إلخ لأن اللفظ لما صار بمنزلة اللباس فالمعنى بمنزلة اللابس ولما كان المعنى اثنين أي الحقيقي ،والمجازي، فاللابسان صار اثنين، يصح التشبيه الذي في المتن؛ لأنه أخذ فيه وحدة اللابس اللهم إلا أن يقال: إن هذا التشبيه ليس في جميع الأشياء، بل في نفس الاستعمال سواء كان اللابس شخصاً أو شخصين لا غير ،فيصح، وإليه أشار الشارح يخليه بقوله: فكما أن استعمال إلخ، ولذا قال الشارح هه ههنا ، والأوضح إلخ، ولم يقل: والصواب تأمل. (القمر) اللابسان إلخ وكل واحد منهما يلبسه بكماله. (القمر) والمعنيان بمنزلة إلخ فالمعنى الحقيقي بمنزلة اللابس بحكم الملك، والمعنى المجازي بمنزلة اللابس بحكم العارية. (القمر) ولا يقال إلخ قلت : ولا يخفى أن هذا الاعتراض يرد على تقرير المصنف ولا يرد على الشارح. (السنبلي) يصدق عليه إلخ فقولكم فكما أن استعمال إلخ مردود. (القمر) حتى يعيره الراهن أي حتى يعير المرتمن الثوب الراهن. (القمر) ولكن بطريق الملك والدليل عليه أنه لو هلك في يد الراهن هلك غير مضمون على المرتمن، و لم يسقط عن دين الرهن شيء. (القمر) كان مانعا أي من استعمال المرهون. (القمر) فإذا أزاله عاد حق المالك إلى أصله ويمكن أن يكون بطريق العارية فقط؛ لأنه لا تظهر لتعلق حق المرتمن ثمرة الملك فيه من البيع والهبة وغيره. ثم شرع المصنف في تفريعات هذه المسألة فقال: حتى قلنا إن الوصية للموالي لا تتناول والي الموالي وإذا كان له معتق واحد يستحق النصف، وتحقيقه أن لفظ المولى مشترك بين المعتق بلا واسطة والمعتق بلا واسطة وقد يطلق على معتق المعتق، وكذا معتق المعتق مجازا، فإذا أوصى رجل لمواليه وله معتق ومعتق جميعًا تبطل الوصية ما لم يبيّن أحدهما؛ دفعًا للاشتراك، وإن لم يكن له معتق بكسر التاء بل معتق ومعتق المعتق على ما هو وضع مسألة المتن يستحق المعتق، ولا يستحق معتق المعتق؛ لأن الموالي حقيقة في المعتق ومجاز في معتق المعتق، فلا يجتمع المجاز مع الحقيقة، فإن كان له معتق واحد يستحق نصف الثلاث؛ لوجود الملابسة فإذا أزاله إلخ أي إذا أزال المرتمن حقه بإجازة الاستعمال عاد حق المالك أي الراهن. (القمر) حق المالك إلخ حتى لو هلك هلك غير مضمون، وما يسقط شيء من الدين. (السنبلي) لأنه لا تظهر إلخ ولأن للمرتهن ولاية الاسترداد إلى يده، ولكونه أحق بالمرهون من سائر الغرماء. (السنبلي) ثمرة الملك فيه إلخ : أي لا يملك الراهن أن يبيع المرهون أو يهبه، فكأنه ليس مالكا ما لم ينفك الرهن. (السنبلي) في تفريعات هذه المسألة أي استحالة إرادة المعنى الحقيقي والمجازي معًا. ثم اعلم أن المصنف عنون التفريعات بقوله: حتى لأن ترتبها على هذه المسألة ثمرتها، وثمرة الشيء غايته كذا قيل. (القمر) يستحق النصف أي نصف الموصى به، سواء كان الموصى به الثلث أو أقل أو أكثر عند الإجازة أو عدم وارث. [فتح الغفار: ١٥٢] أن لفظ المولى إلخ ليس المراد لفظ المولى بدون الإضافة كما يتوهم من ظاهر العبارة، فإن حقيقة لفظ المولى المعتق سواء أعتقه حر الأصل أو المعتق فهو ليس بمجاز في معتق المعتق بل المراد ههنا لفظ المولى إذا كان مضافًا كأن يقال: مولى زيد مثلاً كذا في "التلويح". (القمر) تبطل الوصية : فإن عموم المشترك باطل. (القمر) ومجاز في معتق المعتق إلخ لأن المنسوب إليه حقيقة من يكون منتسبا إليه بالذات وأما معتق المعتق فلا ينسب إليه بالذات (السنبلي) يستحق نصف الثلث إلخ أي والباقي للورثة، وهو قول أبي حنيفة ؛ لأنه أوصى بجماعة الموالي وأقلها اثنان فيكون لكل واحد نصف الوصية، وإذا المولى واحد استحق النصف والباقي ميراث، وعندهما معتق المعتق أيضًا داخل في الوصية لعموم المجاز. (السنبلي)
Explanation of the divisions of the third division: Explanation of the impossibility of combining literal and figurative meaning. It means that the word is to the meaning like the garment is to the person. Figurative is like a borrowed garment, and literal is like an owned garment. Just as using a single garment in one state by way of ownership and borrowing together is impossible, similarly using a single word by way of literal and figurative meaning is impossible. The clearest in the example is to say: just as it is impossible for two persons to wear one garment, one by way of ownership and the other by way of borrowing at one time, so that the word is like the garment and the two meanings are like the two wearers, and literal and figurative are like ownership and borrowing. And it cannot be said: The pledgor, if he borrows the pledged garment from the pledgee and wears it, it can be said of him that he wore it by way of both ownership and borrowing. Because we say: This wearing of his is not by way of borrowing, because the pledgee does not own the garment so that the pledgor borrows it from him, but rather it is by way of ownership, because the right of the pledgee was preventing. So not likewise usage etc. (i.e., it was objected to him from the Shafi'i side: We do not make the word, when intending both literal and figurative meanings, as literal and figurative, so that its usage in both is like using the garment by way of ownership and borrowing. Rather we make it merely figurative, for it is used in each one, and it is not the original meaning. So reflect.) (al-Qamar) And the clearest etc. (i.e., because the word became like the garment, so the meaning became like the wearer; and since there are two meanings, literal and figurative, the wearers became two; the analogy in the text is valid because it assumed unity of the wearer. But it could be said that this analogy is not in all things, but in the very usage whether the wearer is one person or two persons, so it is valid. And the commentator pointed to this with his words: 'Just as usage etc.' Hence the commentator said here: 'and the clearest etc.' and did not say: 'And the correct is to reflect.') (al-Qamar) The two wearers etc.: each one of them wears it completely. (al-Qamar) And the two meanings are like etc.: So the literal meaning is like the wearer by rule of ownership, and the figurative meaning is like the wearer by rule of borrowing. (al-Qamar) And it cannot be said etc.: I say: It is not hidden that this objection applies to the author's presentation and not to the commentator. (al-Sunbuli) It can be said of him etc.: So your statement that 'just as usage etc.' is rejected. (al-Qamar) Until the pledgor borrows it: i.e., until the pledgee lends the garment to the pledgor. (al-Qamar) But it is by way of ownership; the proof is that if it perishes in the pledgor's hand, it perishes without guarantee on the pledgee, and nothing of the debt is reduced. (al-Qamar) Was preventing: i.e., from using the pledged item. (al-Qamar) When he removes it, the owner's right returns to its origin, and it can be only by way of borrowing, because the fruit of ownership does not appear in it due to the attachment of the pledgee's right, such as selling or gifting. Then the author began the branches of this issue and said: So we said: The bequest to mawali does not include the mawla of mawla. And if he has one liberator (mu'tiq), he deserves half. Its verification: The word mawla is homonymous between the liberator without intermediary and the freed slave without intermediary, and it may be used figuratively for the liberator of the liberator, and likewise for the freed slave of the freed slave as a figurative. So if a man makes a bequest to his mawali and he has both a liberator and a freed slave, the bequest is void unless he specifies one, to avoid homonymy. If he does not have a freed slave (freed slave with kasra [mu'taq]) but rather a liberator and a liberator's liberator, as is the premise of the text's issue, the liberator deserves and the liberator's liberator does not deserve, because mawali is literal for the liberator and figurative for the liberator's liberator, so the figurative cannot be combined with the literal. If he has one liberator, he deserves half of the third, due to the connection. (al-Qamar) 'When he removes it etc.': i.e., when the pledgee removes his right by permitting usage, the owner's right returns, i.e., the pledgor. (al-Qamar) 'The owner's right etc.': so that if it perishes, it is without guarantee and nothing of the debt is reduced. (al-Sunbuli) 'Because it does not appear etc.': because the pledgee has the authority to take it back into his hand, and because he is more entitled to the pledged property than other creditors. (al-Sunbuli) 'The fruit of ownership in it etc.': i.e., the pledgor cannot sell the pledged item or give it as a gift, so he is as if not an owner until the pledge is released. (al-Sunbuli) 'In the branches of this issue': i.e., the impossibility of intending literal and figurative meaning together. Then know that the author titled the branches with his word 'until' because their arrangement on this issue is its fruit, and the fruit of a thing is its end, as it is said. (al-Qamar) 'He deserves half': i.e., half of the bequeathed item, whether the bequeathed is one-third or less or more, upon permission or no heir. [Fath al-Ghaffar: 152] 'That the word mawla etc.': It is not intended that the word mawla without addition, as understood from the apparent wording, for the literal meaning of the word mawla is the liberator, whether he freed a free-born person or a freed slave; it is not figurative for the liberator's liberator. Rather what is intended here is the word mawla when it is added, such as saying: the mawla of Zayd, for example. This is in al-Talwih. (al-Qamar) 'The bequest is void': because general application of a homonym is invalid. (al-Qamar) 'And figurative in the liberator's liberator etc.': because the one attributed to is literally one who is attributed by essence, whereas the liberator's liberator is not attributed by essence. (al-Sunbuli) 'He deserves half of the third etc.': i.e., the rest is for the heirs, and this is the saying of Abu Hanifa: because he bequeathed to a group of mawali, and the minimum of them is two, so each gets half of the bequest. And if there is one mawla, he deserves half and the rest is inheritance. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the liberator's liberator is also included in the bequest due to the generality of the figurative. (al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of a usul al-fiqh principle: the impossibility of combining haqiqah (literal meaning) and majaz (figurative meaning) in a single usage of a word. The author uses the analogy of a garment: a single garment cannot simultaneously be owned and borrowed by two persons at the same time. Similarly, a single word cannot be used to convey both its literal and figurative meanings simultaneously. The text then addresses an objection from a Shafi'i scholar, who argues that when intending both meanings, the word is still considered majaz, not a combination. The Hanafi response maintains the impossibility. The passage also applies this principle to a specific fiqh issue: wasiyyah (bequest) using the word 'mawali'. The word 'mawla' is homonymous: it can mean the liberator (mu'tiq) literally, and also the freed slave (mu'taq) literally? Actually the text says mawla is used for the mu'tiq and mu'taq. But in the context of the bequest, it is considered haqiqah for the mu'tiq and majaz for the mu'tiq's mu'tiq. Since haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined, the bequest only goes to the mu'tiq. Abu Hanifa's ruling is that the mu'tiq gets half of the bequest (since there are at least two mawali, so half each), and the remainder goes to the heirs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) include the mu'tiq's mu'tiq as well due to the generality of majaz. This illustrates the practical difference the usul principle makes in fiqh.

Key Terms
الحقيقة (al-haqiqah): The literal, original meaning of a word, like an owned garment in the analogy.
المجاز (al-majaz): The figurative meaning of a word, like a borrowed garment.
المولى (al-mawla): A homonymous word; literally means the liberator (mu'tiq) and the freed slave (mu'taq); figuratively used for the liberator's liberator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man makes a bequest to his 'mawali' and he has one direct liberator (mu'tiq) and one liberator's liberator (mu'tiq al-mu'tiq), who gets the bequest?
A) Both share equally
B) Only the direct liberator gets half
C) Only the indirect liberator gets half
D) The bequest is void

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul principle that haqiqah and majaz cannot be combined determines that a bequest to 'mawali' applies only to the literal meaning (mu'tiq), excluding the indirect liberator.

The Principle: No Combining Literal and Metaphorical Meaning
Explains the impossibility of combining literal and metaphorical meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a word cannot simultaneously carry literal and metaphorical meaning, using the case of extended and non-extended time expressions.

Core Idea
A single utterance cannot be both literal and metaphorical at the same time.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the impossibility of combining literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meanings in one expression. The passage illustrates this through the interpretation of the word 'day' (yawm) in conditional statements, where the meaning depends on whether the connected actions are extended or instantaneous. Understanding this principle is crucial for correctly deriving rulings from sacred texts and everyday speech.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases of combined time expressions
The passage lists three scenarios: both actions extended (e.g., riding and choice), both non-extended (e.g., arrival and manumission), or mixed. For each, the word 'day' is interpreted either literally as daylight or metaphorically as a point in time.
Extended actions take time; non-extended are instantaneous.
2
Determine which meaning is intended in each case
When both are extended, 'day' is literal (daylight). When both are non-extended, 'day' is metaphorical (time). When mixed, the meaning follows the main factor (al-amil).
The rule: 'al-amil' (the operative word) determines the interpretation.
3
Derive the underlying principle
The analysis shows that a single word cannot serve both literal and metaphorical functions simultaneously. The interpreter must choose one based on context and the nature of the connected elements.
This principle applies broadly in usul al-fiqh, e.g., in interpreting oaths and vows.

Source Text

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز ممتدين مثل: "أمرك بيدك يوم يركب زيد" يراد باليوم النهار، وإن كانا غير ممتدين مثل: "عبدي حر يوم يقدم فلان" يراد باليوم الوقت، وإن كان أحدهما ممتداً دون الآخر مثل: "أمرك بيدك يوم يقدم فلان أو أنت طالق يوم يركب زيد"، فالمعتبر هو العامل دون المضاف إليه بالاتفاق. (القمر) يراد باليوم النهار : لأن الأمر باليد أي الاختيار والركوب ممتدان. (القمر) يراد باليوم الوقت لأن حرية العبد أي وقوع العتق على العبد وقدوم فلان غير ممتدين، وكذا وقوع الطلاق على المرأة غير ممتد (القمر) هو العامل: لأنه المقصود دون المضاف إليه، فاعتبار المقصود أولى، قال الشارح في "المنهية" هكذا في حواشي كتب الأصول، ويعلم من شرح الوقاية : أنه ينبغي أن يكون المراد من اليوم حينئذ بياض النهار ترجيحا لجانب الحقيقة. (القمر) وإنما أريد النذر واليمين فيما إذا قال: "لله علي صوم رجب" ونوى به اليمين، جواب سؤال آخر تقريره أن يقال: إذا قال شخص: "الله علي صوم رجب" ونوى به النذر واليمين، أو نوى اليمين فقط، ولم يخطر بباله النذر، فإنه يكون نذراً ويميناً معاً، والنذر معناه الحقيقي، واليمين معناه المجازي، فيلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز معاً، حتى قيل: يلزم بفواته القضاء للنذر، والكفارة لليمين؛ ولهذا قيل: إنه ينبغي أن يقرأ رجب غير منون، ليكون المراد رجب هذه السنة لتظهر ثمرته في الفوات بخلاف ما إذا كان رجباً من العمر، فإنه لا تظهر ثمرته إلا عند الموت بالإيصاء بالفدية، وهذا إنما يرد على أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله، بخلاف أبي يوسف رحمه الله. (القمر) معناه الحقيقي فإن صيغته موضوعة للنذر، ولعدم توقف ثبوته على قرينة النذر. (القمر) واليمين معناه المجازي لتوقف ثبوته على قرينة وهي النية لثبوت النذر، والتوقف على القرينة أمارة المجاز. غير منون فيكون غير منصرف لاجتماع العلمية والعدل عن الرجب؛ لأن المراد الرجب بعينه أي الذي يأتي عقيب اليمين. (القمر) غير منون إلخ : في عبارة فخر الإسلام رجب غير منون للعلمية والعدل عن الرجب المعرف باللام (السنبلي) رجباً أي بتنوين الانصراف لعدم اجتماع السبيين فيه، فإنه لا علمية؛ لأن المراد ليس الرجب المعين. (القمر) وهذا : أي الإيراد بلزوم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) بخلاف أبي يوسف : فإنه عنده لا جمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث فإنه عنده نذر في الأول ويمين في الثاني، وإن لم ينو شيئاً أو نوى النذر مع نفي اليمين، أو بلا نفيه يكون نذراً بالاتفاق، وإن نوى اليمين مع نفي النذر يكون يميناً بالاتفاق، عملاً بنفيه. والإيراد إنما هو على الوجهين الأولين على مذهبهما. فأجاب المصنف بأنه إنما أريد النذر واليمين جميعا في هذه الصورة. لأنه نذر بصيغته، يمين بموجبه، وتحريره: أن قوله: "الله علي" صيغة نذر، وهو معناه الموضوع له، وكان صوم رجب مثلاً قبل النذر مباح الفعل والترك، وبعد النذر صار الفعل واجباً، والترك حراماً، فيلزم من موجب هذا النذر تحريم المباح الذي هو الترك، وتحريم الحلال يمين؛ لأن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم قد حرم مارية أو العسل على نفسه، فسمى الله ذلك يميناً. (القمر) في الأول: أي فيما إذا نوى النذر واليمين. (القمر) في الثاني: أي فيما إذا نوى اليمين فقط. (القمر) أو بلا نفيه أي لم يخطر بباله اليمين. (القمر) يكون نذراً : أي لا يميناً حتى يلزمه القضاء بالفوات دون الكفارة. (القمر) يكون يميناً أي لا نذراً حتى يلزمه الكفارة دون القضاء. (القمر) على الوجهين الأولين: أي ما إذا نوى النذر واليمين أو نوى اليمين ولم يخطر بباله النذر. (القمر) نذر بصيغته لكونها موضوعة لذلك. [فتح الغفار: ١٥٦] فيلزم من موجب إلخ فيه أنه لا يلزم من موجب هذا النذر تحريم الحلال الذي هو الترك، فإنه يكون بالإرادة، بل إنما يلزم منه حرمته، وهذه الحرمة بدون الإرادة لا تكون يميناً وإلا يكون تحريمة الصلاة يميناً بموجبها؛ لأنه يلزمها حرمة المباحات. (القمر) فيلزم إلخ : يعني أن تحريم المباح لازم للنذر لما ثبت في موضعه أن إيجاب الشيء يقتضي تحريم ضده، فأريد اليمين بلازم موجب اللفظ لا باللفظ والنذر أريد باللفظ فيه نظر بينه في شرح "المسلم" فانظر هناك. (السنبلي) موجب فصار النذر موجباً واليمين موجباً. (المحشي) قد حرم مارية أو العسل إلخ: روي أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم خلا بمارية في يوم عائشة أو حفصة رضي الله عنهما، فاطلعت على ذلك حفصة فعاتبته فيه فحرم مارية فنزلت، وقيل: شرب عسلاً عند حفصة فواطأت عائشة وسودة وصفية فقلن له: إنا نشم منك ريح المغافير، فحرم العسل، فنزلت ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ لِمَ تُحَرِّمُ مَا أَحَلَّ اللَّهُ لَكَ تَبْتَغِي مَرْضَاتَ أَزْوَاجِكَ وَاللَّهُ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ (التحريم: ١)، ﴿قَدْ فَرَضَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ تَحِلَّةَ أَيْمَانِكُمْ﴾ (التحريم: ٢) أي قد شرع الله لكم تحليل أيمانكم بالكفارة، كذا قال البيضاوي، والمغافير جمع المغفور بالضم وهو صمغ ذو رائحة كريهة كذا في مجمع البحار. (القمر) أو العسل على اختلاف الروايتين. (المحشي) فسمى الله ذلك يميناً قال ابن الملك في الاستدلال بالآية على أن تحريم المباح يمين نظر؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حلف صريحاً، فإنه قال : والله لا أقربها على ما ذكر في "الكشاف"، فيكون تسميته اليمين بصريح اليمين. (القمر) حلف
A statement of the divisions of the third division. A statement of the impossibility of combining literal and metaphorical. For both extended, like 'Your affair is in your hand on the day Zayd rides' meaning by 'day' the daytime. And if both are non-extended, like 'My slave is free on the day so-and-so arrives' meaning by 'day' the time. And if one is extended and the other not, like 'Your affair is in your hand on the day so-and-so arrives' or 'You are divorced on the day Zayd rides', then the consideration is the factor, not the addressee, by agreement. (Al-Qamar) It intends by 'day' the daytime because the command of the hand, i.e., choice, and riding are extended. (Al-Qamar) It intends by 'day' the time because the freedom of the slave, i.e., the occurrence of manumission upon the slave, and the arrival of so-and-so are non-extended, and likewise the occurrence of divorce upon the woman is non-extended. (Al-Qamar) It is the factor because it is the intended, not the addressee, so considering the intended is prior. The commentator said in 'al-Munyah': thus in the glosses of usul books, and it is known from Sharh al-Wiqayah that the intended from 'day' then should be the brightness of the day, giving preponderance to the side of the literal. (Al-Qamar) And what is intended by the vow and oath when he says: 'For Allah upon me is fasting Rajab' and intends by it the oath, is an answer to another question. Its formulation is: if a person says 'For Allah upon me is fasting Rajab' and intends by it the vow and oath, or intends the oath only and did not think of the vow, then it becomes a vow and oath together. The vow is its literal meaning, and the oath is its metaphorical meaning, so combination of literal and metaphorical is necessary. Thus it is said: upon its failure, qada for the vow and kaffarah for the oath are required. Hence it is said: one should read 'Rajab' without tanwin to mean Rajab of this year, so that its fruit appears upon failure, unlike if it is Rajab of one's lifetime, for its fruit appears only at death and bequest for fidyah. This objection only applies to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), contrary to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). (Al-Qamar) Its literal meaning because its form is placed for the vow, and because its establishment does not depend on a context for the vow. (Al-Qamar) And the oath is its metaphorical meaning because its establishment depends on a context, which is the intention for the establishment of the vow, and dependence on context is a sign of metaphor. Without tanwin, it becomes non-declinable due to the combination of definiteness and alteration from 'al-rajab'; because the intended is the specific Rajab, i.e., one that follows the oath. (Al-Qamar) Without tanwin etc.: in the expression of Fakhr al-Islam, 'Rajab' without tanwin for definiteness and alteration from 'al-rajab' defined by the lam. (al-Sunbuli) 'Rajaban' i.e., with tanwin for declension because the two causes do not combine, as there is no definiteness because the intended is not the specific Rajab. (Al-Qamar) And this: i.e., the objection of necessitating combination of literal and metaphorical. (Al-Qamar) Contrary to Abu Yusuf: for according to him there is no combination of literal and metaphorical. (Al-Qamar) A statement of the impossibility of combining literal and metaphorical. A statement of the divisions of the third division. For according to him it is a vow in the first and an oath in the second, and if he intends nothing or intends the vow with negation of the oath, or without negation, it is a vow by consensus, and if he intends the oath with negation of the vow, it is an oath by consensus, acting on his negation. The objection is only on the first two positions according to their doctrine. So the author answered that only the vow and oath together are intended in this case. Because it is a vow by its wording, an oath by its consequence. Its explanation: that his statement 'For Allah upon me' is a form of vow, and it is its intended meaning, and fasting Rajab for example before the vow was permissible in act and abstention, and after the vow the act became obligatory and abstention prohibited. So from the consequence of this vow follows the prohibition of the permissible which is abstention, and prohibiting the lawful is an oath, because the Messenger (peace be upon him) prohibited Mariyah or honey upon himself, and Allah called that an oath. (Al-Qamar) In the first: i.e., when he intends the vow and oath. (Al-Qamar) In the second: i.e., when he intends the oath only. (Al-Qamar) Or without negation: i.e., he did not think of the oath. (Al-Qamar) It is a vow: i.e., not an oath, so qada for failure is necessary without kaffarah. (Al-Qamar) It is an oath: i.e., not a vow, so kaffarah is necessary without qada. (Al-Qamar) On the first two positions: i.e., when he intends the vow and oath or intends the oath and did not think of the vow. (Al-Qamar) A vow by its wording because it is placed for that. [Fath al-Ghaffar: 156] 'So from the consequence etc.' contains that the prohibition of the lawful which is abstention does not follow from the consequence of this vow, because it is by will, rather only its prohibition follows, and this prohibition without will is not an oath; otherwise the 'tahrimah' of prayer would be an oath by its consequence, because it necessitates the prohibition of permissible acts. (Al-Qamar) 'So from the consequence etc.': means that the prohibition of the permissible is necessary for the vow, as established in its place that making something obligatory necessitates the prohibition of its opposite. So the oath is intended by the necessary consequence of the utterance, not by the utterance, and the vow is intended by the utterance. There is a consideration explained in Sharh al-Muslim, so look there. (al-Sunbuli) The consequence: so the vow becomes a consequence and the oath a consequence. (al-Muhashi) 'He prohibited Mariyah or honey etc.': It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) was alone with Mariyah on the day of Aisha or Hafsa (may Allah be pleased with them), then Hafsa became aware of that and blamed him for it, so he prohibited Mariyah, and it was revealed. And it is said: he drank honey at Hafsa's, and Aisha, Sawda, and Safiyya conspired and said to him: We smell from you the odor of maghafir, so he prohibited honey, and it was revealed: 'O Prophet, why do you prohibit what Allah has made lawful for you, seeking the pleasure of your wives? And Allah is Forgiving, Merciful' (al-Tahrim: 1), 'Allah has already ordained for you the dissolution of your oaths' (al-Tahrim: 2), i.e., Allah has legislated for you the dissolution of your oaths by expiation. Thus said al-Baydawi. And al-maghafir is plural of al-mighfir, with damm, which is a gum with a foul odor. Thus in Majma' al-Bihar. (Al-Qamar) Or honey, according to the two narrations. (al-Muhashi) 'So Allah called that an oath.' Ibn al-Malik said: in using the verse as proof that prohibiting the permissible is an oath, there is consideration, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) swore explicitly, for he said: 'By Allah, I will not approach her,' as mentioned in al-Kashshaf. So his calling it an oath is by explicit oath. (Al-Qamar) He swore.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work discusses the impossibility of combining literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meanings in a single utterance. It first classifies the combination in terms of time expressions: both components are extended (mumtadd), both non-extended, or one extended and one not. The principle is that the meaning is determined by the main factor (al-amil) rather than the time. The text then applies this principle to the case of a person who says 'Lillahi 'alayya sawmu Rajab' (I owe Allah to fast Rajab) intending both a vow (nathr) and an oath (yamin). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, this combines literal and metaphorical meanings: the literal meaning is the vow itself, and the metaphorical meaning is the oath, because the vow necessarily entails prohibiting a permissible action (abstention from fasting), which is the essence of an oath. Therefore, if one fails to fulfill the vow, both qada (making up the fast) and kaffarah (expiation for the oath) are required. To avoid this problematic combination, it is suggested to read 'Rajab' without tanwin to specify the current year. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that no combination occurs; the utterance is either a vow or an oath depending on intention. The text concludes by supporting the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, arguing that the word 'Lillahi 'alayya' is a vow by its wording, and the oath is derived from the necessary consequence of the vow, based on the Quranic verse where Allah called the Prophet's prohibition of honey or Maria an oath.

Key Terms
الحقيقة (al-haqiqah): اللفظ المستعمل فيما وضع له
المجاز (al-majaz): اللفظ المستعمل في غير ما وضع له لعلاقة
اليوم (al-yawm): في هذا السياق: إما النهار (حقيقة) أو الوقت (مجاز)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when both actions are extended (e.g., choice and riding), the word 'day' is interpreted:
A) As a metaphor for the time of the event
B) As literal daytime
C) As both literal and metaphorical simultaneously
D) As dependent on the speaker's intention

Key Takeaway
A single utterance cannot carry both literal and metaphorical meanings; the interpreter must choose one based on context and the main factor.

Vows and Oaths: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Combining Literal and Metaphorical
Explains the application of the principle to vows and oaths with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on combining a vow and oath in one utterance and evaluate the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
A vow is literal; its consequence (prohibiting the permissible) is an oath – but only Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow combining both rulings.

This lesson dives into the practical application of the principle discussed earlier: the case of a person who says 'Lillahi 'alayya sawmu Rajab' intending both a vow and an oath. The passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas, as the choice of ruling affects whether qada, kaffarah, or both are required.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed scenario
A person says 'Lillahi 'alayya sawmu Rajab' and intends both a vow and an oath, or intends the oath only without thinking of the vow.
The wording 'Lillahi 'alayya' is the standard form of a vow.
2
Present Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view
They hold that the utterance is both a vow (literal) and an oath (metaphorical) because the vow's necessary consequence is prohibiting a permissible act, which is the essence of an oath. Therefore, both qada (for the vow) and kaffarah (for the oath) are required.
The vow is literal by its wording; the oath is metaphorical by its consequence.
3
Present Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf argues that no combination is possible. The utterance is either a vow or an oath depending on the speaker's intention. If he intends both, it is not valid as both. If he intends the oath only, it is an oath.
Abu Yusuf adheres strictly to the principle that literal and metaphorical cannot combine.
4
Analyze the evidence and thamarah al-khilaf
The author supports Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, citing the Quranic verse (al-Tahrim 1-2) where Allah calls the Prophet's prohibition of honey an oath. The practical difference (thamarah) is that under the majority view, both qada and kaffarah are wajib; under Abu Yusuf, only one obligation applies.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the concrete difference in rulings.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author (Fakhr al-Islam) chooses the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as reflected in the main text. This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
The tarjih is based on the strength of the dalil (Quran) and the logical connection between vow and oath.

Source Text

بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز ممتدين مثل: "أمرك بيدك يوم يركب زيد" يراد باليوم النهار، وإن كانا غير ممتدين مثل: "عبدي حر يوم يقدم فلان" يراد باليوم الوقت، وإن كان أحدهما ممتداً دون الآخر مثل: "أمرك بيدك يوم يقدم فلان أو أنت طالق يوم يركب زيد"، فالمعتبر هو العامل دون المضاف إليه بالاتفاق. (القمر) يراد باليوم النهار : لأن الأمر باليد أي الاختيار والركوب ممتدان. (القمر) يراد باليوم الوقت لأن حرية العبد أي وقوع العتق على العبد وقدوم فلان غير ممتدين، وكذا وقوع الطلاق على المرأة غير ممتد (القمر) هو العامل: لأنه المقصود دون المضاف إليه، فاعتبار المقصود أولى، قال الشارح في "المنهية" هكذا في حواشي كتب الأصول، ويعلم من شرح الوقاية : أنه ينبغي أن يكون المراد من اليوم حينئذ بياض النهار ترجيحا لجانب الحقيقة. (القمر) وإنما أريد النذر واليمين فيما إذا قال: "لله علي صوم رجب" ونوى به اليمين، جواب سؤال آخر تقريره أن يقال: إذا قال شخص: "الله علي صوم رجب" ونوى به النذر واليمين، أو نوى اليمين فقط، ولم يخطر بباله النذر، فإنه يكون نذراً ويميناً معاً، والنذر معناه الحقيقي، واليمين معناه المجازي، فيلزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز معاً، حتى قيل: يلزم بفواته القضاء للنذر، والكفارة لليمين؛ ولهذا قيل: إنه ينبغي أن يقرأ رجب غير منون، ليكون المراد رجب هذه السنة لتظهر ثمرته في الفوات بخلاف ما إذا كان رجباً من العمر، فإنه لا تظهر ثمرته إلا عند الموت بالإيصاء بالفدية، وهذا إنما يرد على أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله، بخلاف أبي يوسف رحمه الله. (القمر) معناه الحقيقي فإن صيغته موضوعة للنذر، ولعدم توقف ثبوته على قرينة النذر. (القمر) واليمين معناه المجازي لتوقف ثبوته على قرينة وهي النية لثبوت النذر، والتوقف على القرينة أمارة المجاز. غير منون فيكون غير منصرف لاجتماع العلمية والعدل عن الرجب؛ لأن المراد الرجب بعينه أي الذي يأتي عقيب اليمين. (القمر) غير منون إلخ : في عبارة فخر الإسلام رجب غير منون للعلمية والعدل عن الرجب المعرف باللام (السنبلي) رجباً أي بتنوين الانصراف لعدم اجتماع السبيين فيه، فإنه لا علمية؛ لأن المراد ليس الرجب المعين. (القمر) وهذا : أي الإيراد بلزوم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) بخلاف أبي يوسف : فإنه عنده لا جمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) بيان استحالة الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث فإنه عنده نذر في الأول ويمين في الثاني، وإن لم ينو شيئاً أو نوى النذر مع نفي اليمين، أو بلا نفيه يكون نذراً بالاتفاق، وإن نوى اليمين مع نفي النذر يكون يميناً بالاتفاق، عملاً بنفيه. والإيراد إنما هو على الوجهين الأولين على مذهبهما. فأجاب المصنف بأنه إنما أريد النذر واليمين جميعا في هذه الصورة. لأنه نذر بصيغته، يمين بموجبه، وتحريره: أن قوله: "الله علي" صيغة نذر، وهو معناه الموضوع له، وكان صوم رجب مثلاً قبل النذر مباح الفعل والترك، وبعد النذر صار الفعل واجباً، والترك حراماً، فيلزم من موجب هذا النذر تحريم المباح الذي هو الترك، وتحريم الحلال يمين؛ لأن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم قد حرم مارية أو العسل على نفسه، فسمى الله ذلك يميناً. (القمر) في الأول: أي فيما إذا نوى النذر واليمين. (القمر) في الثاني: أي فيما إذا نوى اليمين فقط. (القمر) أو بلا نفيه أي لم يخطر بباله اليمين. (القمر) يكون نذراً : أي لا يميناً حتى يلزمه القضاء بالفوات دون الكفارة. (القمر) يكون يميناً أي لا نذراً حتى يلزمه الكفارة دون القضاء. (القمر) على الوجهين الأولين: أي ما إذا نوى النذر واليمين أو نوى اليمين ولم يخطر بباله النذر. (القمر) نذر بصيغته لكونها موضوعة لذلك. [فتح الغفار: ١٥٦] فيلزم من موجب إلخ فيه أنه لا يلزم من موجب هذا النذر تحريم الحلال الذي هو الترك، فإنه يكون بالإرادة، بل إنما يلزم منه حرمته، وهذه الحرمة بدون الإرادة لا تكون يميناً وإلا يكون تحريمة الصلاة يميناً بموجبها؛ لأنه يلزمها حرمة المباحات. (القمر) فيلزم إلخ : يعني أن تحريم المباح لازم للنذر لما ثبت في موضعه أن إيجاب الشيء يقتضي تحريم ضده، فأريد اليمين بلازم موجب اللفظ لا باللفظ والنذر أريد باللفظ فيه نظر بينه في شرح "المسلم" فانظر هناك. (السنبلي) موجب فصار النذر موجباً واليمين موجباً. (المحشي) قد حرم مارية أو العسل إلخ: روي أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم خلا بمارية في يوم عائشة أو حفصة رضي الله عنهما، فاطلعت على ذلك حفصة فعاتبته فيه فحرم مارية فنزلت، وقيل: شرب عسلاً عند حفصة فواطأت عائشة وسودة وصفية فقلن له: إنا نشم منك ريح المغافير، فحرم العسل، فنزلت ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ لِمَ تُحَرِّمُ مَا أَحَلَّ اللَّهُ لَكَ تَبْتَغِي مَرْضَاتَ أَزْوَاجِكَ وَاللَّهُ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ (التحريم: ١)، ﴿قَدْ فَرَضَ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ تَحِلَّةَ أَيْمَانِكُمْ﴾ (التحريم: ٢) أي قد شرع الله لكم تحليل أيمانكم بالكفارة، كذا قال البيضاوي، والمغافير جمع المغفور بالضم وهو صمغ ذو رائحة كريهة كذا في مجمع البحار. (القمر) أو العسل على اختلاف الروايتين. (المحشي) فسمى الله ذلك يميناً قال ابن الملك في الاستدلال بالآية على أن تحريم المباح يمين نظر؛ لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم حلف صريحاً، فإنه قال : والله لا أقربها على ما ذكر في "الكشاف"، فيكون تسميته اليمين بصريح اليمين. (القمر) حلف
A statement of the divisions of the third division. A statement of the impossibility of combining literal and metaphorical. For both extended, like 'Your affair is in your hand on the day Zayd rides' meaning by 'day' the daytime. And if both are non-extended, like 'My slave is free on the day so-and-so arrives' meaning by 'day' the time. And if one is extended and the other not, like 'Your affair is in your hand on the day so-and-so arrives' or 'You are divorced on the day Zayd rides', then the consideration is the factor, not the addressee, by agreement. (Al-Qamar) It intends by 'day' the daytime because the command of the hand, i.e., choice, and riding are extended. (Al-Qamar) It intends by 'day' the time because the freedom of the slave, i.e., the occurrence of manumission upon the slave, and the arrival of so-and-so are non-extended, and likewise the occurrence of divorce upon the woman is non-extended. (Al-Qamar) It is the factor because it is the intended, not the addressee, so considering the intended is prior. The commentator said in 'al-Munyah': thus in the glosses of usul books, and it is known from Sharh al-Wiqayah that the intended from 'day' then should be the brightness of the day, giving preponderance to the side of the literal. (Al-Qamar) And what is intended by the vow and oath when he says: 'For Allah upon me is fasting Rajab' and intends by it the oath, is an answer to another question. Its formulation is: if a person says 'For Allah upon me is fasting Rajab' and intends by it the vow and oath, or intends the oath only and did not think of the vow, then it becomes a vow and oath together. The vow is its literal meaning, and the oath is its metaphorical meaning, so combination of literal and metaphorical is necessary. Thus it is said: upon its failure, qada for the vow and kaffarah for the oath are required. Hence it is said: one should read 'Rajab' without tanwin to mean Rajab of this year, so that its fruit appears upon failure, unlike if it is Rajab of one's lifetime, for its fruit appears only at death and bequest for fidyah. This objection only applies to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them), contrary to Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). (Al-Qamar) Its literal meaning because its form is placed for the vow, and because its establishment does not depend on a context for the vow. (Al-Qamar) And the oath is its metaphorical meaning because its establishment depends on a context, which is the intention for the establishment of the vow, and dependence on context is a sign of metaphor. Without tanwin, it becomes non-declinable due to the combination of definiteness and alteration from 'al-rajab'; because the intended is the specific Rajab, i.e., one that follows the oath. (Al-Qamar) Without tanwin etc.: in the expression of Fakhr al-Islam, 'Rajab' without tanwin for definiteness and alteration from 'al-rajab' defined by the lam. (al-Sunbuli) 'Rajaban' i.e., with tanwin for declension because the two causes do not combine, as there is no definiteness because the intended is not the specific Rajab. (Al-Qamar) And this: i.e., the objection of necessitating combination of literal and metaphorical. (Al-Qamar) Contrary to Abu Yusuf: for according to him there is no combination of literal and metaphorical. (Al-Qamar) A statement of the impossibility of combining literal and metaphorical. A statement of the divisions of the third division. For according to him it is a vow in the first and an oath in the second, and if he intends nothing or intends the vow with negation of the oath, or without negation, it is a vow by consensus, and if he intends the oath with negation of the vow, it is an oath by consensus, acting on his negation. The objection is only on the first two positions according to their doctrine. So the author answered that only the vow and oath together are intended in this case. Because it is a vow by its wording, an oath by its consequence. Its explanation: that his statement 'For Allah upon me' is a form of vow, and it is its intended meaning, and fasting Rajab for example before the vow was permissible in act and abstention, and after the vow the act became obligatory and abstention prohibited. So from the consequence of this vow follows the prohibition of the permissible which is abstention, and prohibiting the lawful is an oath, because the Messenger (peace be upon him) prohibited Mariyah or honey upon himself, and Allah called that an oath. (Al-Qamar) In the first: i.e., when he intends the vow and oath. (Al-Qamar) In the second: i.e., when he intends the oath only. (Al-Qamar) Or without negation: i.e., he did not think of the oath. (Al-Qamar) It is a vow: i.e., not an oath, so qada for failure is necessary without kaffarah. (Al-Qamar) It is an oath: i.e., not a vow, so kaffarah is necessary without qada. (Al-Qamar) On the first two positions: i.e., when he intends the vow and oath or intends the oath and did not think of the vow. (Al-Qamar) A vow by its wording because it is placed for that. [Fath al-Ghaffar: 156] 'So from the consequence etc.' contains that the prohibition of the lawful which is abstention does not follow from the consequence of this vow, because it is by will, rather only its prohibition follows, and this prohibition without will is not an oath; otherwise the 'tahrimah' of prayer would be an oath by its consequence, because it necessitates the prohibition of permissible acts. (Al-Qamar) 'So from the consequence etc.': means that the prohibition of the permissible is necessary for the vow, as established in its place that making something obligatory necessitates the prohibition of its opposite. So the oath is intended by the necessary consequence of the utterance, not by the utterance, and the vow is intended by the utterance. There is a consideration explained in Sharh al-Muslim, so look there. (al-Sunbuli) The consequence: so the vow becomes a consequence and the oath a consequence. (al-Muhashi) 'He prohibited Mariyah or honey etc.': It is narrated that he (peace be upon him) was alone with Mariyah on the day of Aisha or Hafsa (may Allah be pleased with them), then Hafsa became aware of that and blamed him for it, so he prohibited Mariyah, and it was revealed. And it is said: he drank honey at Hafsa's, and Aisha, Sawda, and Safiyya conspired and said to him: We smell from you the odor of maghafir, so he prohibited honey, and it was revealed: 'O Prophet, why do you prohibit what Allah has made lawful for you, seeking the pleasure of your wives? And Allah is Forgiving, Merciful' (al-Tahrim: 1), 'Allah has already ordained for you the dissolution of your oaths' (al-Tahrim: 2), i.e., Allah has legislated for you the dissolution of your oaths by expiation. Thus said al-Baydawi. And al-maghafir is plural of al-mighfir, with damm, which is a gum with a foul odor. Thus in Majma' al-Bihar. (Al-Qamar) Or honey, according to the two narrations. (al-Muhashi) 'So Allah called that an oath.' Ibn al-Malik said: in using the verse as proof that prohibiting the permissible is an oath, there is consideration, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) swore explicitly, for he said: 'By Allah, I will not approach her,' as mentioned in al-Kashshaf. So his calling it an oath is by explicit oath. (Al-Qamar) He swore.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul al-fiqh work discusses the impossibility of combining literal (haqiqah) and metaphorical (majaz) meanings in a single utterance. It first classifies the combination in terms of time expressions: both components are extended (mumtadd), both non-extended, or one extended and one not. The principle is that the meaning is determined by the main factor (al-amil) rather than the time. The text then applies this principle to the case of a person who says 'Lillahi 'alayya sawmu Rajab' (I owe Allah to fast Rajab) intending both a vow (nathr) and an oath (yamin). According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, this combines literal and metaphorical meanings: the literal meaning is the vow itself, and the metaphorical meaning is the oath, because the vow necessarily entails prohibiting a permissible action (abstention from fasting), which is the essence of an oath. Therefore, if one fails to fulfill the vow, both qada (making up the fast) and kaffarah (expiation for the oath) are required. To avoid this problematic combination, it is suggested to read 'Rajab' without tanwin to specify the current year. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that no combination occurs; the utterance is either a vow or an oath depending on intention. The text concludes by supporting the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, arguing that the word 'Lillahi 'alayya' is a vow by its wording, and the oath is derived from the necessary consequence of the vow, based on the Quranic verse where Allah called the Prophet's prohibition of honey or Maria an oath.

Key Terms
النذر (al-nathr): إيجاب شيء على النفس بصيغة مخصوصة
اليمين (al-yamin): تحريم الحلال باليمين أو الحلف
القضاء (al-qada): أداء الفعل الفائت أو المكروه
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): جزاء مالي أو بدني لتكفير الذنب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the thamarah al-khilaf between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in the vow/oath case?
A) Abu Hanifa/Muhammad require only qada; Abu Yusuf requires only kaffarah
B) Abu Hanifa/Muhammad require both qada and kaffarah; Abu Yusuf requires one depending on intention
C) Abu Hanifa/Muhammad require only kaffarah; Abu Yusuf requires both
D) Both agree on requiring both qada and kaffarah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) allows combining a literal vow and a metaphorical oath from its consequence, requiring both qada and kaffarah.
